GEN/28
CIRCUMSTANCES OF OFFENCE(S)

At 3pm Saturday 15th April 1989police Officers were on duty at the junction of the North
Stand and Lappings Lane end of Hillsbro Football Ground,Sheffield•At this location P C
1785 Cheetham   became aware of a youth climbing over"a fence at that location.The officer
went to him and as   he did so he became   aware that the youth had fallen from the railing c
onto the seats.As the officer attempted to deal with the youth the surrounding fans began
to shout threats and obscenities at him,they also spat at him.The officer went to seek
medical assistance and as he walk down the stand became aware of fans fromM    the Leppings
Lane end jumping over the railings onto-the pitch.lt was apparent that s canething was
occuring in that area.In the congestion on the stand the officer was pushed forwards by
the accused who shouted "THATS A BIT FUCKING Sr
                                              j?KONG".The officer turned around and took
hold of the accised and he began to struggle with him.The officer had no choice but to
attempt to restrain Him but such was the ferocity of him two other officers nearby assistec
M m and he was forcibly taken to the police room*On detention the offieer resumed to other
obvious duties.
He was later verbally cautioned at the ground.




A. L. Cheetham. PC 1785.

CIRCUMSTANCES OF OFFENCE(S)

Offences

1) On Saturday, 15th April, 1989* at Sheffield, did unlawfully possess cannabis 8®sd@,
   being a Class 'B1 controlled drug as specified in Schedule 2 of the Misuse of Drugs
   Act, 1971.

   Contrary to : Section 5 (2) of the Misuse of Drugs Act, 1971*

2) On 15th April, 1989, whilst drunk did attempt to enter the Sheffield Wednesday Football
   Ground, Hillsborough, Sheffield, that being a designated sports ground during the period
   of a designated sporting event, viz a Football Association Challenge Cup semi final
   match, between Nottingham Forest and Liverpool.        ' -

   Contrary to : Section 2 of the Sporting Events (Control of Alcohol etc.) Act, 1985*

Circumstances of Offences

   On Saturday, 15th April, 1989, a Football Association Challenge Cup semi final match
   between Nottingham Forest and Liverpool was due to take place at Sheffield Wednesday
   Football Ground, Sheffield.

   At 2.20pm on this date Police Constable 2278 VARLEY was on duty in company with Police
   Constable V? MOLE in Penistone Road North, Sheffield, outside the football ground.

   At this time a man known now to be the defendant              was seen in Penistone Road
   North on the far side of the carriageway to the ground. As the officers watched the
   defendant he was seen to stagger across the carriageway towards the ground and then stand
   by a turnstile entrance with an admission ticket to the match in his hand.

   Police Constable VARLEY went to the defendant as he was about to enter the    ground throug
   the turnstile and drew him to one side. The officer then noticed that                 I
   breath smelled strongly of intoxicants, that his speech was slurred, his eyes glazed,
   and that he was unsteady on his feet. The officer was of the opinion that
   was drunk.           *                                  .

                 was arrested and taken to the Police Detention Room within the ground
   where he was documented and searched. At this point the defendant was found to have in
   his possession a small polythene bag containing what appeared to be seeds. When questioned
   he admitted that the seeds were cannabis.

   The defendant was subsequently reported for the above offences

CIRCUMSTANCES OF OFEENCE(S)




At 2.20pm on Saturday 15th April 1989 Police Constable 2278 Varley was on uniform
foot patrol in Pennistone Road, Sheffield, outside the Hilsborough Football Stadium.
His duties were to supervise the football fans arriving for the FA Cup football
semi-final due to take place at 3«00pm that afternoon between Liverpool and Nottingham
Forest football clubs.


The officer's attention was drawn to the defendant                who staggered across
Pennistone Road and joined a queue to enter the ground. He approached and asked the
defendant to come to one side. This he did and the officer immediately noticed his
breath smelled strongly of intoxicants, his eyes were glazed, his speech slurred and
he was unsteady on his feet, he was drunk.

In view of this               Jwas arrested for attempting to enter a designated
football ground whilst drunk. He was cautioned replying that he was from            and
just wanted to go in and see the football match.


The defendant was then taken to the police room where he was documented and during
searching)______________ (produced a small plastic bag from his pocket which he stated
contained canabis seeds. He was therefore placed under arrest for this also and
was detained.


Due to the occurence of the 'Hilsborough Football Disaster1                was gxven
an instant verbal caution for these offences and was released.

CIRCUMSTANCES OF OFFENCE(S)

             At 3.00pm Saturday 15th April 1989 an F.A. cup Semi Final football
match commenced at Sheffield Wednesday Football ground Hillsborough Sheffield
between Nottingham Forest and Liverpool. Nottingham Forest supporters were
accomodated at the Penaistone Road or Kop end of the ground and Liverpool supporters
war® seated in the North Stapad.
             At approximatly 3 «06pm that afternnon after the match had been in progress
about 6 minutes there was a disturbance at the leppings lane end of the ground involving
    "’■J               . :' ' t; V '              ■.                                 j 1
Liverpool supporters which resulted in the game being stopped and the players taken from
                        o . o o v   vi ■                                               "        '    -    o    '
the field.A large number of police officers went over to the Leppings Lane end of the
ground and fans spilled onto the pitch at that end of the ground.
             At about 3 *12pm that afternnon the accused                                                                who was seated in the
North Stand was seen to leave his seat and make his wasj to the front gangway near to
the Kop end of that stand. At this time he started to shout towards the Nottingham
Foreet supporters at the Kop end and he was waving his arms in an agrresive manner
while making gestures towards them. He was heard to shout ’’YOUR ALL A SET OF BASTARDS
SO FUCKIN SHUT UP CUNTS".
             Nottingham Forest supporters near to the front end of the Kop near the
North stand were reacting to                      actions and they moved towards the front perimeter
fence. There appeared to be 25 to 30 fans on the Kop end who reacted and they started
to climb on the front perimeter fenee as they were shouting and making agresive gestures
towards the ac^sfid*m           c>fUf0 . _ri   ' ' CO.   7        ..rr        ' J   , r >'7                        J-           r         _Q
J IT j.QI            was°approSch«d at 3*15piJi that afternooii by ta Police -Officer in
                                        [ c              i   j:          .c                \/       _. r _ r _ - s      o *   c iq   -'   ;    y   .   o '   rf
uniform who tgld ftim ^e waf under arrest ,.for £n offence^of threatening behaviour.After
Sauticim lie 'replied nTHEYRE JUSTxA SET 0F-[BA£TARDSh.°He was taken to the,,Police roomo
situated behind the North Stand of the ground where he arrived at 3.17pm. He was
documented, photographed then detained.
              Later that eveing he was verbally cautioned for the offence before
 being released.
